<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">Antennas can be seamlessly integrated into clothing by means of embroidery with conductive thread. In the real-life applications, wearable antennas are exposed to various environmental conditions. We studied the impact of moisture and washing on the performance of fully functional RFID tags based on embroidered antennas. The moisture absorbed in the tag structure can cause a temporary reduction in the tag read range. Repeated washing of the tag resulted in permanent reduction, which accumulated over the wash repetitions. Overall, the results indicated that protective coating is needed for sustained operation. Flexible, durable, and hydrophopic polymers, such as polydimethylsiloxane (PDMS), and polymer-ceramic composites are prominent candidates in terms of mechanical and electromagnetic properties.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Passive radio frequency identification (RFID) technology provides the automatic identification and tracking of items. This is achieved by labeling the items with battery-free remotely addressable tags composed of an antenna and an integrated circuit (IC). Electromagnetic waves at ultra-high frequencies (UHF) provide a means for powering and communicating with passive tags, which enables rapid interrogation of a large quantity of tags through various media from the distances of several meters. Currently, passive UHF RFID systems are used in access control, supply chain management, and in item-level asset tracking, while new applications are continually emerging. For instance, RFID sensors based on antenna self-sensing and low-power integrated sensors have gained much attention <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Miniature, ultra-low-power, and maintenance-free tags are also envisioned to provide platforms for wireless sensor nodes in the next generation internetâthe internet of things <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. In addition, a variety of biomedical applications from detecting limb movement to miniature RFID-inspired neural recording tags are being investigated <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>.</p><p>Lightweight and conformal electrotextiles based on conductive threads and fabrics <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a> provide compelling means to fabricate seamlessly garment-integrated antennas. This technology has huge potential in RFID, wireless body-area networks, and body-centric sensing systems, for instance. However, the durability of electrotextile antennas in real-life applications is an important issue to be addressed before the deployment of this technology in the applications <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>. In this letter, the effects of moisture and washing procedures on the performance of fully functional passive UHF RFID tags equipped with embroidered antennas are studied.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Fabrication of the Embroidered Tags</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> shows a fabricated prototype tag. The tag antenna is a T-matched straight dipole, which we studied earlier in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a>. The antenna is composed of conductive thread (Shieldex 110f34 dtex 2-ply HC <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>), which is made of two strands of conductive fiber. The polyamide filament cores in each strand are plated with 99% pure silver. The thread has dc resistance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 8.952em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">500</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Â±</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">100</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-16" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-18"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">500~\Omega /{\hbox{m}} \pm 100~\Omega /</script></tex-math></inline-formula>m, but the antenna RF properties depend strongly on the sewing pattern and stitch density. The mechanical properties of the thread are such that it can be used in standard embroidery fabrication. We used a computer-aided sewing machine (Husqvarna VIKING) to embroider the antenna on cotton fabric (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-21" role="math" style="width: 11.234em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 10.093em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1010.03em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-24" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Îµ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-25"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-27" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-29" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.8</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">tan</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-33"></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-34" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.183em;">Î´<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.018</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\varepsilon_{\rm r} = 1.8,~\tan\delta = 0.018</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a>) with the thickness of approximately 0.25 mm. This way, the antenna is seamlessly integrated into clothing, for instance, without introducing additional equipment to the textile manufacturing process.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>Fabricated embroidered RFID tag studied in this letter.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6677514/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>After embroidery fabrication of the tag antennas, we equipped them with ISO 18000-6 compliant tag ICs in order to perform wireless testing of fully functional embroidered RFID tags. The IC is NXP UCODE G2iL series IC (wake-up power: â18 dBm). The manufacturer had mounted the chip in a fixture patterned from copper on a plastic film. We attached the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-37" role="math" style="width: 5.228em; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-41" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">3</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.99em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-44"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-45"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-46"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-47" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; <div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Measurement Method</h2></div><p>The maximum distance at which a tag can be detected by a reader is an important practical tag performance indicator. Using the theoretical read range to evaluate the performance of RFID tags also has the advantage that it can be measured wirelessly when the tag IC is operable and connected to the antenna. This way, the problematic invasive small antenna measurements are avoided and separate characterization of the tag IC is not required.</p><p>Normally, the read range of passive tags is limited by the wireless power transfer from the reader to the tag IC. Assuming free-space conditions for site-independent comparison, the direct line of sight read range is given by <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3">[11]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-51" role="math" style="width: 100%; Voyantic Tagformance RFID measurement system was employed to record the threshold power over a range of frequencies. The measurement system illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>.

In this formulation, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-460" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.38em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-461"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-462"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-463" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-464"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-465"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-466" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-467" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">P_{\rm th}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> implicitly includes the possible polarization mismatch power loss. However, in the measurement, we used a linearly polarized transmit antenna aligned for polarization matching with the measured dipole tags.</p><p>In free-space conditions, at the critical transmit-antennaâtag separation, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-468" role="math" style="width: 3.907em; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-471" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-472" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-474"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-475"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-476" style="font-size: 70.7%; Correspondingly, the incident power density is equal to the threshold power density. vertical-align: -1.463em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 3.537em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-28">d_{\rm tag}= \sqrt {{{\rm EIRP} \over {4\pi \;S_{\rm inc,th}}}}= {\lambda\over {4\pi}}\sqrt {{{\rm EIRP} \over {L_{\rm iso} P_{\rm th}}}} \eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">d_{\rm tag}= \sqrt {{{\rm EIRP} \over {4\pi \;S_{\rm inc,th}}}}= {\lambda\over {4\pi}}\sqrt {{{\rm EIRP} \over {L_{\rm iso} P_{\rm th}}}} \eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</span></span></disp-formula>which is an estimate of the theoretical read range of the tag. In practice, the properties of the transmit-antennaâtag wireless channel vary from site to site. Thus, in order to provide a universal characterization, we chose to evaluate the tags in terms of the free-space read range. All the measurement results presented below were obtained following the RFID emission regulation in Europe: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-641" role="math" style="width: 6.55em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.889em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1005.65em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-642"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-643" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">E</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-644" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">I</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-645" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-646" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">P</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-647" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-648" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-649"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-650" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3.28</span></span></span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-651" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">\rm EIRP ={3.28}~</script></tex-math></inline-formula> W.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Results and Discussion</h2></div><p>To evaluate the impact of moisture on the tag performance, the tag was thoroughly wetted with tap water and measured the threshold power at short time intervals until the tag was dry. To evaluate the impact of washing, we washed the tags repeatedly in a household washing machine with different washing programs and measured the threshold power after each wash. The results are presented in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4a" class="fulltext-link">Sections IV-A</a> and <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4b" class="fulltext-link">IV-B</a>.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Impact of Moisture</h3><p>We measured the threshold power of a wet tag at 4-min time intervals until it was dry. The experiment was done in room temperature. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a> shows the tag read range <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-652" role="math" style="width: 2.646em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.345em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.23em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-653"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-654" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-655"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-656" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-657"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-658"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-659" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-660" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-661" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-662" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">(d_{\rm tag})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> computed from the measurement results as explained in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III</a>. The tag exhibits broadband characteristics.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 3. </b><fig><p>Read range versus frequency every 24 min during drying.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6677514/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As seen from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a>, within the 840â960-MHz frequency band, the tag operated well in the nominal dry conditions, but <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-663" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-664"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-665"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-666" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-667"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-668"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-669" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-670" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-671" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">d_{\rm tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reduced due to moisture. This is because the added water content in the cotton fabric increased its permittivity detuning the antenna and the additional dielectric loss introduced by the water reduced the antenna radiation efficiency. These phenomena are due to the high dielectric constant and loss tangent of water in comparison to textile structures <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_4a">[12]</a>. Below 830 MHz, however, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-672" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.57em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-673"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-674"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-675" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-676"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-677"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-678" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-679" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-680" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">d_{\rm tag}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increased due to moisture. Here, we need to recall that originally the tag was designed for the 840â960-MHz range. Therefore, it is possible that outside this range, the water content in the tag structure modified the antenna impedance toward better matching with the tag IC. As seen from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a>, this improves the read range if the radiation efficiency reduces relatively less. Since the geometry of the antenna remained unchanged during the wetting test, we expect that the possible change in the antenna directivity was negligible. As a summary, the decrease in the read range due to moisture was 1.3, 1.1, and 0.70 m at the frequencies of 866, 915, and 954 MHz, respectively, and the tag maintained its broadband characteristics. In comparison, an electrotextile patch antenna on a cotton fabric substrate suffered from a notable shift in its operation frequency due to moisture <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_4a">[12]</a>. Finally, we observed that after drying, the tag performance returned to the original. This confirmed that the tag IC was not damaged during wetting. Hence, we were assured that the observed changes in the read range were due to the moisture in the antenna structure alone.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Impact of Washing</h3><p>The tags were washed using detergent and three different washing programs listed in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a>. The washed tags had the tag ICs on them during washing. The threshold power of the washed tags was measured after each wash after the tags had completely dried. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 4</a>â<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6</a> show the tag read ranges versus the number of wash repetitions at lower, middle, and upper frequencies of the global UHF RFID frequency band. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a> shows read range (computed from the measurement results as explained in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III</a>) of the tags versus frequency after an even number of Type-1 washes.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>Washing Programs Used in Testing<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>Read range versus wash repetitions at 866.6 MHz for three tags washed in different programs.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6677514/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Read range versus wash repetitions at 954.2 MHz for three tags washed in different programs.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6677514/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 7. </b><fig><p>Read range versus frequency for various amount of washes in Type-1 program.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6677514/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As seen from the results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 4</a>â<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6</a>, the read range reduced after each wash for all the studied washing programs. Moreover, as seen from <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a>, the harshness of the washing conditions (temperature, rotational speed, and the amount of detergent) increased toward Type-3 washing. This corresponds with the more rapid decrease in read range versus the number of wash repetitions in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 4</a>â<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6</a>. Overall, we attributed the performance drop to the dissolution of conductive material from the embroidered antennas, which reduced the antenna radiation efficiency. This is supported by the fact that a complete breakage of the conductive thread would likely have resulted in a much more drastic performance drop than the gradual reduction seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. It was also noticed that after one to three washes, the tag IC became dysfunctional (possibility of failure in the epoxy-joint was excluded by reattachment) regardless of the washing program. Thus, we needed to replace the tag IC in between wash repetitions.</p><p>In addition, it was noticed that the decrease in the read range to be approximately linear (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 4</a>â<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">7</a>) regardless of the used washing procedure and frequency. By extrapolating the obtained read range versus the number of wash repetitions, an estimation was made on how many wash repetitions <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-681" role="math" style="width: 1.805em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.5em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-682"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-683" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-684" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-685" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">(N)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> bring the read range below 50 cm, which was considered here as a minimum for practical applications. The results at 866 MHz are presented in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ II</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Estimated Reduction in <span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-686" role="math" style="width: 2.054em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.591em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.59em 2.649em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-687"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-688"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.591em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.53em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-689" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.532em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-690"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-691"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-692" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-693" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-694" style="font-size: 70.7%; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.413em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.421em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">d_{\rm tag}</script> at 866 MHz and the Number of Wash Repetitions (<span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-695" role="math" style="width: 1.128em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.863em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1000.86em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-696"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-697" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">N</script>) Bringing <span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-698" role="math" style="width: 2.054em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.591em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1001.59em 2.649em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-699"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-700"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.591em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.53em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-701" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.532em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-702"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-703"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-704" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-705" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-706" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">g</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.413em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.421em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">d_{\rm tag}</script> Below 50 cm<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6677514/6677514-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table II" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>Finally, due to variability in the embroidery fabrication, the â144 minâ result in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 3</a> and âInitialâ result in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a> are not identical, and before washing in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 4</a>â<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6</a>, one of the tags exhibits higher read range than the other two. These level shifts are comparable to the impact of one washing cycle in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. Discussions and Potential Remedies</h3><p>The results from the wetting test showed that moisture did not result in a significant performance drop, and after drying, the tag operation returned to original. In washing cycles, the performance of the plain uncoated embroidered antennas decreased over the wash repetitions. This was attributed to the dissolution of the conductive material from the embroidered antenna. Coating the antenna in a flexible, hydrophobic, and durable material, such as polydimethylsiloxane (PDMS) or thermoplastic polyurethane (TPU) has been proposed to protect electrotextile antennas in washing cycles <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_4c">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_4c">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_4c">[13]</a>. Flexible polymer-ceramic composites achieving high permittivity could be utilized in antenna miniaturization at the same time <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_4c">[7]</a>. The coating will also protect the tag IC. On the other hand, small encapsulated chip-sized UHF RFID tags intended for harsh environments <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_4c">[14]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_4c">[15]</a> can be proximity-coupled to a larger electrotextile antenna body to avoid the problematic ICâtextile joint.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>Embroidery fabrication provides compelling means for wearable antennas. We investigated the impact of moisture and washing on fully functional passive UHF RFID tags based on embroidered antennas. First, an embroidered tag was wetted, and its performance was monitored until it had dried. In this test, up to 1.3-m temporary drop in tag read range was found due to antenna detuning and reduced radiation efficiency. Second, the embroidered tags were washed in a household washing machine in different washing programs. An accumulating reduction in tag read range was observed over the wash repetitions. This was attributed to dissolution of the conductive material. Based on the test data, it was estimated that depending on the harshness of the washing program, the tag read range would drop below 50 cm after 7â23 wash repetitions. This suggests that protective coating is needed for sustained operation. In the future, coating materials will be investigated further to determine an optimal choice in terms of mechanical and electromagnetic properties and fitness for integration with textiles in mass production.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank Dr. A. Ali Babar from the Department of Electronics and Communications Engineering, Tampere University of Technology, Tampere, Finland, for valuable discussions.</p></div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
